UCSDOffersFeministTheaterOass 
Two new literature courses focuslIlg on the 

"margIllS- of theater have been added to the Fall 
class schedule. ViSIting Professor Katrtn Sleg Will 
teach -Women In Theater" and "Modem Theater 
thiS quarter. 

"Women III Theater IS an upper diVISion course 
exarnllllng a ' femlllist look at theater." said Sieg. 
She Will take four different feminist approaches to 
theater during the course: radical. materialistic, 
lesbian, and finally a non-gender de filled look. 

"Modern Theater ' Will go "more IIltO the 
margins of modern theater. " Sleg explained. The 
upper-divlsion class will look at some of the less 
traditional and "more challenging" plays. 

Sieg joined the UCSD Theater department last 
Spring but lost her Job In the budget cuts that went 
through thiS summer. She Will be teaching in the 
Literature Department in the Fall and Winter 
quarters. 

Women 's Studies Department Chair Stephanie 
Jed said that she was pleased to have Sieg 
teaching at UCSD. ·We have never had a feminist 
theater critiC on the campus .. . theater IS a vital 
area of feminist expression." she said. 

New Earth Sciences Major 
In conjunction With the SCriPPS Institution of 

Oceanography. UCSD will start a new academic 
program In the Earth SCiences thiS Fall . 

Focusing on the evolution of the earth as a 
system and on the underlYing processes and 
dynamiCS, It has a specifiC emphaSIS on prOViding 
a solid foundation In mathematics. physics. and 
chemistry. 

According to 510 Director Edward A. Frieman, 
the program stresses the study of the earth as a 
total system of physical, geological. and chemical 

processes interacting on a global scale. Faculty will 
use the entire planet - land. oceans, and atmo-
sphere - as a classroom for students and as a 
laboratory for a broad spectrum of basic science 
research. 

The program Includes a wide range of academic 
activities ranglllg from field work and data collection 
to computer modeling. 

The new academiC program also prOVides for an 
Earth SCiences minor. 

UCSD To Lead Alzheimer's Study 
UCSD School of MediCine will direct the first 

clinical drug trial on moderately demented 
Alzheimer's patients, and witll the help of interpret-
ers. on Spanish-speaking Alzheimer's patients as 
well. 

Last week. researchers at 23 centers across the 
country began recruiting patients to test the effective-
ness of selegeline (Deprenyl) and tocopherol (vitamin 
E) at slowing the progression of Alzheimer's disease. 

UCSD Neurosciences Professor Leon Thai, M.D .. 
will lead the study. 

It is the first trial to be conducted by the 
Alzheimer's Disease Cooperative Study Unit, a 3()' 
center national consortium established by the 
National Institute on Aging in October 1991 with aid 
from a five-year. $18 million grant to the UCSD 
School of Medicine. 

No large scale study has ever been conducted on 
the effectiveness of Deprenyl on Alzheimer's 
patients, although the drug is currently approved by 
the federal government for the treatment of 
Parklnson 's disease. 

ApprOXimately 370 Alzheimer's patients with 
moderate dementia will be enrolled in the two-year 
tnal.

Academic Services 
Monday through Friday 
. 8 a.m .-4:30 p.m. - The OASIS Writing 
Center is a free service for all UCSD 
students. We offer one-to-one writing con-
ferences for any type of writing project -
academic papers, personal statements, 
even stories and poems. Our staff of 
trained undergraduates , who come from a 
variety of academic disciplines , can help 
you become a more effective writer. Call 
534-2284 to make an appointment or 
drop by our office in the old Student Cen-
ter, Building B, Room 214. 
. 8 a.m.-4:30 p.m. (Friday 3 p.m.) - The 
OASIS Language Program provides assis-
tance to those dOing work in Japanese, 
German, Spanish. French and Vietnam-
ese. A diagnostic test on written English is 
avai lable on request. Call 534-2284 for 
more informat ion . 
• 8 :30 a.m.-4:30 p.m. - Let OASIS 
Study Management Center help you this 
quarter with time managemen t, note tak-
ing and editing, textbook analysis , memory, 
flexible/ speed reading, vocabulary devel-
opment and GRE/ LSAT / MCATverbal com-
prehension. Stop by York Hall 4010 or call 
534-7344 to set up a personal appoint-
ment. Also - stay on the lookout forthose 
valuable OASIS Study Skills Workshop and 
the GRE weekend specials. 

Services/Workshops 
Monday-Friday 
.8 a.m.-2 p.m. - SIGI+ Computer-based 
program of career information designed 
to help you clarify your skills, valu~s and 
interest. For more information, come to 
the Career Services Center. $10. 
• 1:30-4 p.m. - DROP-IN ADVISING 
HOURS - For help with career goals, job 
hunting, resume preparation , or exploring 
professional or graduate school opportu-
nities. No appointment needed, just walk 
in to the Career Services Center. 
Tuesday, Sept. 29 
• 1 :30 p.m. - MARKETABLE RESUME 
- Learn how to make a positive first 
impression with your resume atthe Career 
Services Center. 
Wednesday, Sept. 30 
• 11 a.m.-12:3n p.m. - GRADUATE 
SUPPORT GROUP: A group for men and 
women graduate students experiencing 
frustration, fear, disappointment and lone-
liness in their graduate programs. Leader: 
Hugh Pates, 534-3456. Revelle College 
Provost's Building. 
.2 p.m. - INTERVIEWING SKILLS WORK-
SHOP - Learn techniques required to be 
successful in the interview process. Ca-
reer Services Center. 
Thursday, Oct. 1 
.11 a.m. - JOB SEARCH 101 - 80% of 
all job vacancies are unadvertised. This 
workshop will teach you the most effective 
way to find them. At the Career Services 
Center. 
.12-1:30 p.m. - PAN-ASIAN COMMU-
NITY FORUM: Drop-in group addressing 
concerns of Asian/Pacific Islander stu-
dents. Leaders: Jeanne Manese, 543-
3035, and Alvin Alavarez. Mountain View 
Lounge .

Tuesday-Saturday 
• 10 a,m.-5 p.m. (Saturday -2 p.m.) -
"Personal Visions" show at the Grove 
Gallery focuses on "outsider" art in an 
exhibition of several personal works, in-
cluding that of Howard Finster, Mose 
Toliver, Mamie Deschillie and Patrick Davis. 
Local San Diegans Pete Taylor and Robert 
DeAndrea will partiCipate in the folk art 
show, which continues through Oct. 24,

tive college students are expected to tour 
UCSD during the annual Preview Day. 
Presentations will also be given on hous-
ing, fin ancia l aid, academics, campus li fe 
and student organizations.

NOTICE 
ALLOCATION OF SPACE 

Room 2.307 (approx . .468 sq. ft.) Price Center 
(Formerly utilized by the 

Woman's Resource Center) 

The University Center Board is accepting requests 
from student organizations and University units who 

primarily serve students, to use the space on an 
annual allocation basis. 

Written requests will be accepted through 4pm, 
October the 12th, 1992 

Address requests stating need, purpose, etc ... to 
Aaron Goodman/Vice-Chair, University Center 

Board, 0076, Price Center, or drop them off at the 
Reservation desk at the Price Center 2nd Aoor, East.
